## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a chemical concentration A, which is the standard setup for kinetic rate-law modeling via ordinary differential equations. With only (t, A) available, plausible structures are concentration-dependent rate laws (orders, autocatalysis, inhibition) and/or explicit time-dependent driving (e.g., time-varying rate coefficients).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate formation or depletion under saturation/constant feed)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (unimolecular decay/growth; c0 < 0 for decay)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or pseudo-second-order behavior)
- General n-th order power law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting)
- Linear source–sink: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (constant feed plus first-order loss; chemostat-like lumping)
- Reversible approach to equilibrium (linear relaxation): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (net rate proportional to distance from equilibrium concentration)
- Autocatalytic logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with depletion/limitation)
- Cubic/quenching term (higher-order termination): dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 - c2 * A**3 (production with bimolecular/trimolecular loss or radical recombination)
- Product-inhibited rate (rational inhibition): dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) (effective rate reduced at high A due to self-inhibition/limited accessibility)
- Rational decay (finite-time blow-down avoidance): dA_dt = -c0 / (A + c1) (phenomenological slowing as A decreases; regularized near A=0)
- Time-dependent first-order coefficient (aging/catalyst decay): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate constant changes exponentially in time due to temperature program or catalyst deactivation/activation)
- Periodic forcing in rate coefficient: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 + sin(c2 * t)) * A (externally modulated kinetics, e.g., light/duty-cycle driven reactions)
- Parallel pathways (sum of orders): dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (two concurrent mechanisms contributing to net rate)
- Mixed explicit time and concentration: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A**c2 (empirical time-varying kinetics, e.g., evolving environment or catalyst sites)
- Implicit equilibrium with nonlinear driving: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) * A**c2 (approach to equilibrium with order-dependent dependence on A)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Straight line in A vs t suggests near zero-order (dA_dt approximately constant over the observed range).
- Exponential-in-time A(t) (linear in log(A) vs t) indicates first-order kinetics dA_dt ∝ A.
- If 1/A vs t is approximately linear, that supports second-order kinetics dA_dt ∝ -A**2.
- A non-integer best-fit exponent in dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 often reflects lumped mechanisms, chain reactions, or changing effective order.
- Presence of a stable nonzero fixed point (dA_dt = 0 at A = c1) suggests relaxation-to-equilibrium forms like c0 * (c1 - A) or autocatalytic limitation c0 * A * (c1 - A).
- If rates diminish at high A (sublinear growth of |dA_dt| with A), rational inhibition forms like c0 * A / (A + c1) can encode crowding/self-inhibition.
- If kinetics accelerate or decelerate over time at the same A, explicit time dependence in the rate coefficient (e.g., exp(c*t), t**c) is a key structural cue.
- Sign changes in dA_dt over time or with A can indicate competing source/sink terms (e.g., c0 + c1*A or c0*A - c1*A**2) rather than a single-order law.
- Multiple curvature regimes in plots of dA_dt vs A often suggest parallel pathways (sum of powers) rather than a single power law.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK32)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_f*A**c4
Candidate formulas: 71

GT is the fixed function
\[
F(t,A)=0.7991114344496316\,A^{1/3}-0.4994732695791710\,A-0.4994732695791710\,A\,e^{-0.050569865727257013\,t}.
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **exactly three terms**: an \(A^{1/3}\) term (no \(t\)), an \(A\) term (no \(t\)), and an \(A e^{kt}\) term with \(k=-0.05056\ldots\), and **no other dependence** (no constants, no logs/sqrts/ratios/Abs unless they can be removed by setting coefficients to 0, etc.).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether extra structures can be zeroed out and whether the remaining structures can match the three GT terms.

---

### 1
Has \(A^2\), sqrt\(\cdot e^{c5 t}\), and log terms. You can zero sqrt/log terms by setting their coefficients to 0, but then you still have \(A^2 c0 + A c1 + c2\), which cannot produce \(A^{1/3}\) nor \(A e^{kt}\). **No match.**

### 2
Has \(A^2\), log term \(A^{c2}c3\log(Ac4+1)\), sqrt\(\cdot e^{c8 t}\). Even if you zero log and sqrt terms, you get \(A^2 c0 + A c1 + c5\), missing \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A e^{kt}\). **No match.**

### 3
Contains \(A^{1/3}c0\) and \(A c1\) (good), but the exponential term is \(c5 e^{c6 t}\,|A|\) (uses \(|A|\), not \(A\)). To equal GT for all real \(A\), you’d need \(|A|=A\) for all \(A\), impossible. Setting that coefficient to 0 removes the needed \(A e^{kt}\) term. Also has a rational-in-\(A\) term and constant. **No match.**

### 4
Has \(A^2\), \(A e^{c3 t}\), \(A^{c4} e^{c6 t}\), and \(e^{A c8}\). Even if you zero unwanted terms, you cannot get an \(A^{1/3}\) term without also having \(t\)-dependence on it (since the only power term is multiplied by an exponential). **No match.**

### 5
Form: \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A^{c3} c4 e^{c5 t} + c6 e^{A c7} + c8\).
To get \(A^{1/3}\) independent of \(t\), you’d need \(c5=0\) so \(e^{c5 t}=1\), and \(c3=1/3\). Then set \(c6=0, c8=0\). Remaining:
\(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + c4 A^{1/3}\).
This can match GT by choosing:
- \(c4=0.7991114344496316\)
- \(c0=-0.4994732695791710\)
- \(c1=-0.4994732695791710\)
- \(c2=-0.050569865727257013\)
So **this candidate can match**.

### 6
Has \(A^{c3}c4\) (good for \(A^{1/3}\)), and \(A c1 e^{c2 t}\) (good), but also has \(c5 e^{A c6}\) and \(c8 e^{A c9}\) and constant \(c7\). Set \(c5=0, c8=0, c7=0\). Then choose \(c3=1/3\) and match coefficients as in #5. **Match possible.**

### 7
Has \(A^{1/3}c0\), \(A c1\), and **two** \(A\cdot e^{(\cdot)t}\) terms: \(A c2 e^{c3 t} + A c4 e^{c5 t}\), plus constant \(c6\).
Set one exponential coefficient to 0 (e.g., \(c4=0\)), set \(c6=0\), then match remaining \(A^{1/3}\), \(A\), and \(A e^{kt}\) terms by choosing \(c3=-0.05056\ldots\) and coefficients accordingly. **Match possible.**

### 8
Has \(A^{1/3}c0\), \(A c1\), \(A c2 e^{c3 t}\), plus \(c4 e^{c5 t}|A|\). The \(|A|\) term must be removed (set \(c4=0\)) to work for all real \(A\). Then it becomes \(A^{1/3}c0 + A c1 + A c2 e^{c3 t} + c6\). Set \(c6=0\) and match coefficients/exponent. **Match possible.**

### 9
Has \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t}\) but the power term is a saturating rational \(A^{c3}c4/(A^{c3}+c5)\), not \(A^{1/3}\). No way to make that equal \(A^{1/3}\) for all \(A\) by constants (unless you do degenerate things like \(c5=0\) giving a constant \(c4\), still not \(A^{1/3}\)). Also has \(e^{A c7}\). **No match.**

### 10
Has \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A^{c3}c4 + c5 + c6/(A+c7)\).
You can set \(c6=0\), \(c5=0\), choose \(c3=1/3\), and match coefficients/exponent. **Match possible.**

### 11
Has \(|A|\) exponential and log in \(|A|\); cannot produce \(A e^{kt}\) without \(|A|\), and cannot remove log unless coefficient 0, but still lacks \(A e^{kt}\) with plain \(A\). **No match.**

### 12
Has \(A^2\) term and \(A^{c4}c5\) (good), and \(A c2 e^{c3 t}\) (good), but also \(e^{A c7}\) and constant. Set \(c0=0\), \(c6=0\), \(c8=0\), choose \(c4=1/3\), and match coefficients/exponent. **Match possible.**

### 13
Has \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t}\) and \(A^{c5}c6\) (can be \(A^{1/3}\)), but also \(A c3/(A+c4)\) which cannot be identically 0 for all \(A\) unless \(c3=0\). Do that, set \(c7=0\), choose \(c5=1/3\), match. **Match possible.**

### 14
Has \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t}\) plus constant and log term; no \(A^{1/3}\) term. **No match.**

### 15
Has \(A^{c1}c2 e^{c3 t}\) and \(|A|e^{c5 t}\) and an extra \(e^{c5 t}\) term. To get \(A^{1/3}\) independent of \(t\) you could set \(c3=0\) and \(c1=1/3\), but then you still need an \(A\) (non-exponential) term, which is absent. Also \(|A|\) issue. **No match.**

### 16
Has \(|A|e^{c3 t}\) and a log-in-\(t\) term; cannot form \(A e^{kt}\) with plain \(A\) for all real \(A\). **No match.**

### 17
\(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t} + c6\).
Set \(c5=0\), \(c3=1/3\), \(c6=0\), then match coefficients/exponent. **Match possible.**

### 18
Has \(A^{1/3}c0\), \(A c1\), \(A c2 e^{c3 t}\), plus \(A c4/(A+c5)\) (must set \(c4=0\)) and constant (set \(c6=0\)). Then match. **Match possible.**

### 19
Has \(|A|e^{c5 t}\) term; must set its coefficient \(c4=0\). Then remaining includes \(A c2/(A+c3)\) which must be removed by \(c2=0\). Then you lose the needed \(A e^{kt}\) term entirely (since no other exponential-in-\(t\) with \(A\)). **No match.**

### 20
Has \(A c0\) and \(A^{c1}c2 e^{c3 t}\) plus sqrt term; no separate \(A\) and \(A e^{kt}\) simultaneously unless you use the same term, but then you can’t also get \(A^{1/3}\) without \(t\)-dependence. **No match.**

### 21
Has correct base pieces \(A^{1/3}c0 + A c1 + A c2 e^{c3 t}\) plus constant and log term. Set log coefficient \(c5=0\), set \(c4=0\), then match. **Match possible.**

### 22
Has \(|A|e^{c3 t}\) and a power of \(|A|\); cannot represent plain \(A e^{kt}\) for all real \(A\). **No match.**

### 23
\(A^{1/3}c0 + A c1 + A c2 + A c3 e^{c4 t} + c5\).
Combine \(A c1 + A c2\) into one \(A\) coefficient by choosing them to sum to \(-0.49947...\). Set \(c5=0\). Match \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A e^{kt}\) via \(c3, c4\). **Match possible.**

### 24
Has \(|A|e^{c4 t}\) instead of \(A e^{kt}\); must set that term to 0, then no exponential term remains. **No match.**

### 25
\(A^{1/3}c0 + A c1 + A c2 e^{c3 t} + c4\). Set \(c4=0\) and match coefficients/exponent. **Match possible.**

### 26
Has \(|A|e^{c3 t}\) not \(A e^{kt}\); cannot match for all real \(A\). **No match.**

### 27
\(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A^{c3}c4 + c5\). Set \(c5=0\), choose \(c3=1/3\), match coefficients/exponent. **Match possible.**

### 28

### 29
Has sqrt\(\cdot e^{c5 t}\) and constant; no \(A\) exponential term of form \(A e^{kt}\), and sqrt cannot become \(A\) for all \(A\). **No match.**

Has \(A c0 + A^{c1}c2\) and sqrt term; no \(A e^{kt}\) term. **No match.**

### 33
Has \(|A|e^{c3 t}\) and log; cannot match \(A e^{kt}\) for all real \(A\). **No match.**

### 34
Has \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t}\) plus a rational term and a \(1/(A+c7)\) term. You can set those extra coefficients \(c4=0\) and \(c6=0\), but then you still lack an \(A^{1/3}\) term. **No match.**

### 35
Same issue as 34: no \(A^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 36

### 37

To get \(A e^{kt}\), set the other to power 1 and \(c3=-0.05056...\). Then match \(A\) linear term via \(A c0\). Set constant \(c7=0\). **Match possible.**

### 38
Has log term; removable by setting its coefficient \(c7=0\). Then it’s like #17 with an extra constant \(c6\) removable by \(c6=0\). Choose \(c5=0\), \(c3=1/3\), match. **Match possible.**

### 39
\(A c0 + A^{c1}c2 e^{c3 t} + A^{c4}c5 + c6\).
Set \(c6=0\). Choose \(c4=1/3\) for the \(A^{1/3}\) term. For the exponential term, choose \(c1=1\) and \(c3=-0.05056...\) to get \(A e^{kt}\). Then match \(A\) via \(A c0\). **Match possible.**

### 40
\(A^{1/3}c0 + A c1 + A c2 e^{c3 t} + A^{c4}c5 + c6\).
To avoid an extra independent power term, set \(c5=0\). Set \(c6=0\). Then match as in #25. **Match possible.**

### 41
Has an \(A^{c2}\log(Ac4+1)\) term and \(|A|e^{c6 t}\). Even if you zero those, you’re left with \(A^{1/3}c0 + A c1 + c7\), missing \(A e^{kt}\). **No match.**
